<p><b>Pope Alexander VI</b>, born <b>Rodrigo de Borja</b> (<a href="/wiki/Valencian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a>: <span lang="ca-valencia" xml:lang="ca-valencia"><i><b>Roderic Llançol i <a href="/wiki/Borgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Borgia">de Borja</a></b></i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[roðeˈɾiɡ ʎanˈsɔɫ i ðe ˈβɔɾdʒa]</a></span>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es" xml:lang="es"><i><b>Rodrigo Lanzol y de Borja</b></i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[roˈðɾiɣo lanˈθol i ðe ˈβorxa]</a></span>; 1 January 1431&#160;– 18 August 1503), was <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> from 11 August 1492 until his death. He is one of the most controversial of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> popes, partly because he acknowledged fathering several children by his mistresses. Therefore his Italianized Valencian surname, <i><a href="/wiki/Borgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Borgia">Borgia</a></i>, became a byword for <a href="/wiki/Libertine" title="Libertine">libertinism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nepotism" title="Nepotism">nepotism</a>, which are traditionally considered as characterizing his pontificate. Two of Alexander's successors, the controversial pontiffs <a href="/wiki/Sixtus_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Sixtus V">Sixtus V</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban VIII">Urban VIII</a>, described him as one of the most outstanding popes since <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_family">Birth and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Birth and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rodrigo de Borja was born on 1 January 1431, in the town of <a href="/wiki/Xativa" class="mw-redirect" title="Xativa">Xativa</a> near <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>, one of the component realms of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>, in what is now Spain. His parents were <a href="/wiki/Jofr%C3%A9_Llan%C3%A7ol_i_Escriv%C3%A0" title="Jofré Llançol i Escrivà">Jofré Llançol i Escrivà</a> (died bef. 24 March 1437), and his Aragonese wife and distant cousin Isabel de Borja y Cavanilles (died 19 October 1468). His family name is written Llançol in <a href="/wiki/Valencian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a> and Lanzol in Castillian (Spanish). Rodrigo adopted his mother's family name of <a href="/wiki/Borgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Borgia">Borja</a> in 1455 following the elevation to the <a href="/wiki/Papacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Papacy">papacy</a> of maternal uncle Alonso de Borja (Italianized to Alfonso Borgia) as <a href="/wiki/Calixtus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Calixtus III">Calixtus III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alternatively, it has been argued that Rodrigo's father was Jofré de Borja y Escrivà, making Rodrigo a Borja from his mother and father's side.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> However, his children were known to be of Llançol paternal lineage. Some revisionists suggest that the confusion is attributed by attempts to connect Rodrigo as the father of Giovanni, Cesare, Lucrezia, and Gioffre, who were surnamed <i>Llançol i Borja</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rodrigo Borgia studied law at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">Bologna</a> where he graduated, not simply as <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">Doctor of Law</a>, but as "the most eminent and judicious jurisprudent".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> After the election of his uncle as <a href="/wiki/Pope_Callixtus_III" title="Pope Callixtus III">Pope Callixtus III</a>, he was ordained <a href="/wiki/Deacon" title="Deacon">deacon</a> and created <a href="/wiki/Lay_cardinal" title="Lay cardinal">Cardinal-Deacon</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/San_Nicola_in_Carcere" title="San Nicola in Carcere">San Nicola in Carcere</a></i> at the age of twenty-five in 1456. The following year, he was appointed <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Chancery" title="Apostolic Chancery">vice-chancellor</a> of the Holy Roman Church. Both <a href="/wiki/Nepotism" title="Nepotism">nepotistic</a> appointments were characteristic of the age. Each pope during this period inevitably found himself surrounded by the servants and retainers of his predecessors who often owed their loyalty to the family of the pontiff who had appointed them.<sup id="cite_ref-Burkle_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkle-9">[8]</a></sup> In 1468, he was ordained to the <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_(Catholic_Church)" class="mw-redirect" title="Priesthood (Catholic Church)">priesthood</a> and, in 1471, he was consecrated bishop and appointed <a href="/wiki/Cardinal-Bishop_of_Albano" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal-Bishop of Albano">Cardinal-Bishop of Albano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CE1913_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE1913-1">[1]</a></sup> Having served in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a> under five popes – his uncle Calixtus III, <a href="/wiki/Pius_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius II">Pius II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_II" title="Pope Paul II">Paul II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sixtus_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Sixtus IV">Sixtus IV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Innocent_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Innocent VIII">Innocent VIII</a> – Rodrigo Borgia acquired considerable administrative experience, influence and wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_and_personality">Appearance and personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Appearance and personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Contemporary accounts suggest that Rodrigo was "handsome, with a very cheerful countenance and genial bearing. He was gifted with the quality of being a smooth talker and of choice eloquence. Beautiful women were attracted to him and excited by him in quite a remarkable way, more strongly than how 'iron is drawn to a magnet'."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Rodrigo Borgia was also an intelligent man with an appreciation for the arts and sciences and an immense amount of respect for the Church. He was capable and cautious, considered a "political priest" by some. He was a gifted speaker and great at conversation. Additionally, he was "so familiar with Holy Writ, that his speeches were fairly sparkling with well-chosen texts of the Sacred Books".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[Note 2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[Note 3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg/220px-Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg" width="220" height="406" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg/330px-Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg/440px-Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="2980" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaque_Borja_Valencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Plaque outside the Archbishop's Palace, Valencia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archbishop_of_Valencia">Archbishop of Valencia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Archbishop of Valencia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When his uncle Alonso de Borja (<a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Valencia_in_Spain" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Valencia in Spain">bishop of Valencia</a>) was elected Pope Callixtus III, he "inherited" the post of bishop of Valencia. Sixteen days before the death of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_VIII" title="Pope Innocent VIII">Pope Innocent VIII</a>, he proposed Valencia as a <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitan</a> <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">see</a> and became the first archbishop of Valencia. When Rodrigo de Borgia was elected pope as Alexander VI following the death of Innocent VIII, it was the turn of his son <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Borgia" title="Cesare Borgia">Cesare Borgia</a> to "inherit" the post as second archbishop of Valencia. The third and the fourth archbishops of Valencia were <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Borja_Lanzol_de_Roman%C3%AD,_el_menor" title="Juan de Borja Lanzol de Romaní, el menor">Juan de Borja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Luis_de_Borja" title="Pedro Luis de Borja">Pedro Luis de Borja</a>, grand-nephews of Alexander VI.</p>
<p>Translation of the plaque on the side of the Archbishop's Palace of Valencia:</p>
<blockquote>
<center>
<p>ALEXANDER VI<br />
The 9th July 1492, Pope Innocent VIII, at the request of Cardinal Borja and the Catholic Monarchs, raised the Valencian See to the rank of metropolitan, making Rodrigo of Borja the first Archbishop of Valencia<br />
1492 - 1503</p>
</center>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mistresses_and_family">Mistresses and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mistresses and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg/220px-Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg/330px-Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg/440px-Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg 2x" data-file-width="732" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vannozza_Cattanei.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vannozza_dei_Cattanei" title="Vannozza dei Cattanei">Vannozza dei Cattanei</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Of Alexander's many mistresses the one for whom passion lasted longest was <a href="/wiki/Vannozza_dei_Cattanei" title="Vannozza dei Cattanei">Vannozza (Giovanna) dei Cattanei</a>, born in 1442, and wife of three successive husbands. The connection began in 1470, and she had four children whom he openly acknowledged as his own: <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Borgia" title="Cesare Borgia">Cesare</a> (born 1475), <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Borgia,_2nd_Duke_of_Gandia" title="Giovanni Borgia, 2nd Duke of Gandia">Giovanni</a>, afterwards duke of <a href="/wiki/Gandia" title="Gandia">Gandia</a> (commonly known as Juan, born 1476), <a href="/wiki/Lucrezia_Borgia" title="Lucrezia Borgia">Lucrezia</a> (born 1480), and <a href="/wiki/Gioffre_Borgia" title="Gioffre Borgia">Gioffre</a> (Goffredo in Italian, born 1481 or 1482).</p>
<p>For a period of time, before legitimizing his children after becoming Pope, Rodrigo pretended that his four children with Vannozza were his niece and nephews and that they were fathered by Vannozza's husbands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Before his elevation to the papacy, Cardinal Borgia's passion for Vannozza somewhat diminished, and she subsequently led a very retired life. Her place in his affections was filled, according to some, by the beautiful <a href="/wiki/Giulia_Farnese" title="Giulia Farnese">Giulia Farnese</a> ("<i>Giulia la Bella</i>"), wife of an <a href="/wiki/Orsini_family" title="Orsini family">Orsini</a>. However, he still very dearly loved Vannozza, in a way he considered 'spiritual', and his love for his children by Vannozza remained as strong as ever and proved, indeed, the determining factor of his whole career. He lavished vast sums on them and lauded them with every honor. Vannozza lived in the Palace of a late Cardinal, or in a large, palatial villa. The children lived between their mother's home and the Papal Palace itself. The atmosphere of Alexander's household is typified by the fact that his daughter Lucrezia apparently lived with Giulia at a point.<sup id="cite_ref-Villari_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villari-17">[14]</a></sup></p>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 176px">

</ul>
<p>Four other children, Girolama, Isabella, <a href="/wiki/Pier_Luigi_de_Borgia,_1st_duke_of_Gand%C3%ADa" title="Pier Luigi de Borgia, 1st duke of Gandía">Pedro-Luiz</a>, and Bernardo, were of uncertain maternal parentage. His daughter Isabella was the great-great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_X" title="Pope Innocent X">Pope Innocent X</a>, who was therefore descended in a direct line from Alexander.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg/220px-DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg/330px-DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg/440px-DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1983" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DomenichinounicornPalFarnese.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Giulia_Farnese" title="Giulia Farnese">Giulia Farnese</a> as – <i>A young Lady and a <a href="/wiki/Unicorn" title="Unicorn">Unicorn</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Domenichino" title="Domenichino">Domenichino</a>, ca 1602, from <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Farnese" title="Palazzo Farnese">Palazzo Farnese</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A daughter, Laura, was born to his mistress, <a href="/wiki/Giulia_Farnese" title="Giulia Farnese">Giulia Farnese</a>; paternity was officially attributed to <a href="/wiki/Orsino_Orsini" title="Orsino Orsini">Orsino Orsini</a> (Farnese's husband). He is an ancestor of virtually all royal houses of Europe, mainly the southern and western ones, for being the ancestor of <i>Dona</i> <a href="/wiki/Luisa_de_Guzm%C3%A1n" title="Luisa de Guzmán">Luisa de Guzmán</a>, wife of King <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">John IV of Portugal</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Election">Election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_1492" title="Papal conclave, 1492">Papal conclave, 1492</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:164px;max-width:164px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo,_Rome.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Alexander VI – Castel Sant'Angelo, Rome." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG/160px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG" width="160" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG/240px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG/320px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Pope_Alexander_VI_Borgia_-_Castel_Sant%27Angelo%2C_Rome.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2070" data-file-height="2439" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Coat of Arms of Alexander VI – Castel Sant'Angelo, Rome</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There was change in the constitution of the College of Cardinals during the course of the fifteenth century-especially under Sixtus IV and Innocent VIII. Of the twenty-seven cardinals alive in the closing months of the reign of Innocent VIII no fewer than ten were <a href="/wiki/Cardinal-nephews" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal-nephews">Cardinal-nephews</a>, eight were crown nominees, four were Roman nobles and one other had been given the cardinalate in recompense for his family's service to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>; only four were able career churchmen.<sup id="cite_ref-Burkle_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkle-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the death of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_VIII" title="Pope Innocent VIII">Pope Innocent VIII</a> on 25 July 1492, the three likely candidates for the <a href="/wiki/Papacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Papacy">Papacy</a> were the sixty-one-year-old Borgia,<sup id="cite_ref-Burkle_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkle-9">[8]</a></sup> seen as an independent candidate, <a href="/wiki/Ascanio_Sforza" title="Ascanio Sforza">Ascanio Sforza</a> for the Milanese, and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Giuliano della Rovere</a> seen as a pro-French candidate. It was rumoured but not substantiated that Borgia succeeded in buying the largest number of votes and Sforza, in particular, was bribed with four mule-loads of silver.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[17]</a></sup> Mallett shows that Borgia was in the lead from the start and that the rumours of bribery began after the election with the distribution of benefices; Sforza and della Rovere were just as willing and able to bribe as anyone else.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[18]</a></sup> The benefices and offices granted to Sforza, moreover, would be worth considerably more than four mule-loads of silver. <a href="/wiki/Johann_Burchard" title="Johann Burchard">Johann Burchard</a>, the conclave's master of ceremonies and a leading figure of the papal household under several popes, recorded in his diary that the <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_1492" title="Papal conclave, 1492">1492 conclave</a> was a particularly expensive campaign. Della Rovere was bankrolled to the cost of 200,000 gold <a href="/wiki/Ducat" title="Ducat">ducats</a> by <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">King Charles VIII of France</a>, with another 100,000 supplied by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Burchard_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burchard-23">[19]</a></sup> Borgia was elected on 11 August 1492, assuming the name of Alexander VI (due to confusion about the status of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Pope Alexander V">Pope Alexander V</a> elected by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Pisa" title="Council of Pisa">Council of Pisa</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_di_Lorenzo_de%27_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Giovanni di Lorenzo de' Medici">Giovanni di Lorenzo de' Medici</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a>) is said to have warned after the election, "Now we are in the power of a wolf, the most rapacious perhaps that this world has ever seen. And if we do not flee, he will inevitably devour us all."<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[20]</a></sup> Such a criticism, particularly by the very youthful Giovanni, is believed to be highly unlikely: "Precocious though he was, the cardinal would scarcely have made this observation when sixteen years of age."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[21]</a></sup> Even if he did make the comment, though, <a href="/wiki/Michael_de_la_B%C3%A9doy%C3%A8re" title="Michael de la Bédoyère">Michael de la Bédoyère</a> says that it would be "unintentionally complimentary as coming from a representative of one of the leading Italian States about a Pope whose aim it would be to save Italy in defiance of the prejudices and jealousies of its petty rulers".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_in_office">Early years in office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early years in office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_(FindID_53537).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg/220px-Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg/330px-Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg/440px-Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_%28FindID_53537%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1761" data-file-height="902" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lead_papal_bulla_of_Alexander_VI_(FindID_53537).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Papal_bulla" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal bulla">Papal bulla</a> of Alexander VI</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In contrast to the preceding pontificate, Pope Alexander VI adhered initially to strict administration of justice and orderly government. Before long, though, he began endowing his relatives at the church's and at his neighbours' expense. <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Borgia" title="Cesare Borgia">Cesare Borgia</a>, his son, while a youth of seventeen and a student at <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a>, was made <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Valencia" title="Province of Valencia">Valencia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Borgia,_2nd_Duke_of_Gandia" title="Giovanni Borgia, 2nd Duke of Gandia">Giovanni Borgia</a> inherited the Spanish Dukedom of <a href="/wiki/Gandia" title="Gandia">Gandia</a>, the Borgias' ancestral home in Spain. For the Duke of Gandia and for <a href="/wiki/Gioffre_Borgia" title="Gioffre Borgia">Gioffre</a>, also known as Goffredo, the Pope proposed to carve fiefs out of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a>. Among the fiefs destined for the duke of Gandia were <a href="/wiki/Cerveteri" title="Cerveteri">Cerveteri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anguillara" class="mw-redirect" title="Anguillara">Anguillara</a>, lately acquired by <a href="/wiki/Virginio_Orsini" title="Virginio Orsini">Virginio Orsini</a>, head of that powerful house. This policy brought <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Naples" title="Ferdinand I of Naples">Ferdinand I, King of Naples</a>, into conflict with Alexander, who was also opposed by Cardinal della Rovere, whose candidature for the papacy had been backed by Ferdinand. Della Rovere fortified himself in his <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ostia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Ostia">bishopric of Ostia</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a>'s mouth as Alexander formed a league against Naples (25 April 1493) and prepared for war.<sup id="cite_ref-Villari_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villari-17">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand allied himself with <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. He also appealed to Spain for help, but Spain was eager to be on good terms with the papacy to obtain the title to the recently discovered <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. Alexander, in the bull <i><a href="/wiki/Inter_Caetera" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter Caetera">Inter Caetera</a></i> on 4 May 1493, divided the title between Spain and Portugal along a demarcation line. This became the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a> which was ratified by Spain on 2 July 1494 and by Portugal on 5 September 1494. (This and other related bulls are known collectively as the <i><a href="/wiki/Bulls_of_Donation" title="Bulls of Donation">Bulls of Donation</a></i>.)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="French_involvement">French involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: French involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italy_1494_AD.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Italy_1494_AD.png/220px-Italy_1494_AD.png" width="220" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Italy_1494_AD.png/330px-Italy_1494_AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Italy_1494_AD.png/440px-Italy_1494_AD.png 2x" data-file-width="1261" data-file-height="1805" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italy_1494_AD.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Italy 1494</div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(April 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Pope Alexander VI made many alliances to secure his position. He sought help from <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">Charles VIII of France</a> (1483–1498), who was allied to <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_Sforza" title="Ludovico Sforza">Ludovico "Il Moro" Sforza</a> (the Moor, so called because of his swarthy complexion), the <i>de facto</i> Duke of Milan, who needed French support to legitimise his rule. As King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Naples" title="Ferdinand I of Naples">Ferdinand I of Naples</a> was threatening to come to the aid of the rightful duke <a href="/wiki/Gian_Galeazzo_Sforza" title="Gian Galeazzo Sforza">Gian Galeazzo Sforza</a>, the husband of his granddaughter <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Aragon,_Duchess_of_Milan" title="Isabella of Aragon, Duchess of Milan">Isabella</a>, Alexander encouraged the French king in his plan for the conquest of Naples.</p>
<p>But Alexander, always ready to seize opportunities to aggrandize his family, then adopted a double policy. Through the intervention of the Spanish ambassador he made peace with Naples in July 1493 and cemented the peace by a marriage between his son Gioffre and <a href="/wiki/Sancha_of_Aragon" title="Sancha of Aragon">Doña Sancha</a>, another granddaughter of Ferdinand I.<sup id="cite_ref-Burchard_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burchard-23">[19]</a></sup> In order to dominate the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Cardinals" title="College of Cardinals">Sacred College of Cardinals</a> more completely, Alexander, in a move that created much scandal, created 12 new cardinals. Among the new cardinals was his own son Cesare, then only 18 years old. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Alessandro Farnese</a> (later Pope Paul III), the brother of one of the Pope's mistresses, <a href="/wiki/Giulia_Farnese" title="Giulia Farnese">Giulia Farnese</a>, was also among the newly created cardinals.</p>
<p>On 25 January 1494, Ferdinand I died and was succeeded by his son <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_II_of_Naples" title="Alfonso II of Naples">Alfonso II</a> (1494–1495).<sup id="cite_ref-Burchard_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burchard-23">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">Charles VIII of France</a> now advanced formal claims on the Kingdom of Naples. Alexander authorised him to pass through Rome, ostensibly on a <a href="/wiki/Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusade">crusade</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, without mentioning Naples. But when the French invasion became a reality Pope Alexander VI became alarmed, recognised Alfonso II as king of Naples, and concluded an alliance with him in exchange for various fiefs for his sons (July 1494). A military response to the French threat was set in motion: a Neapolitan army was to advance through the <a href="/wiki/Romagna" title="Romagna">Romagna</a> and attack Milan, while the fleet was to seize <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. Both expeditions were badly conducted and failed, and on 8 September Charles VIII crossed the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> and joined Ludovico il Moro at Milan. The Papal States were in turmoil, and the powerful <a href="/wiki/Colonna" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonna">Colonna</a> faction seized <a href="/wiki/Ostia_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostia (district)">Ostia</a> in the name of France. Charles VIII rapidly advanced southward, and after a short stay in Florence, set out for Rome (November 1494).</p>
<p>Alexander appealed to <a href="/wiki/Ascanio_Sforza" title="Ascanio Sforza">Ascanio Sforza</a> and even to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultan</a> <a href="/wiki/Bayazid_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayazid II">Bayazid II</a> for help. He tried to collect troops and put Rome in a state of defence, but his position was precarious. When the Orsini offered to admit the French to their castles, Alexander had no choice but to come to terms with Charles. On 31 December, Charles VIII entered Rome with his troops, the cardinals of the French faction, and Giuliano della Rovere. Alexander now feared that Charles might depose him for <a href="/wiki/Simony" title="Simony">simony</a>, and that the king would summon a council to nominate a new pope. Alexander was able to win over the <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Bri%C3%A7onnet_(Cardinal)" title="Guillaume Briçonnet (Cardinal)">bishop of Saint-Malo</a>, who had much influence over the king, with a cardinal's hat. Alexander agreed to send Cesare as legate to Naples with the French army; to deliver <a href="/wiki/Cem_Sultan" class="mw-redirect" title="Cem Sultan">Cem Sultan</a>, held as a hostage, to Charles VIII, and to give Charles <a href="/wiki/Civitavecchia" title="Civitavecchia">Civitavecchia</a> (16 January 1495). On 28 January Charles VIII departed for Naples with Cem and Cesare, but the latter slipped away to <a href="/wiki/Spoleto" title="Spoleto">Spoleto</a>. Neapolitan resistance collapsed, and Alfonso II fled and abdicated in favour of his son <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Naples" title="Ferdinand II of Naples">Ferdinand II</a>. Ferdinand was abandoned by all and also had to escape, and the Kingdom of Naples was conquered with surprising ease.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="French_in_retreat">French in retreat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: French in retreat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(April 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A reaction against Charles VIII soon set in, for all the European powers were alarmed at his success. On 31 March 1495 the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1495)" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy League (1495)">Holy League</a> was formed between the Pope, the emperor, <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_il_Moro" class="mw-redirect" title="Ludovico il Moro">Ludovico il Moro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand of Spain</a>. The League was ostensibly formed against the Turks, but in reality it was made to expel the French from Italy. Charles VIII had himself crowned King of <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> on 12 May, but a few days later began his retreat northward. He met the League at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fornovo" title="Battle of Fornovo">Fornovo</a> and cut his way through them and was back in France by November. Ferdinand II was reinstated at <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> soon afterwards, with Spanish help. The expedition, if it produced no material results, demonstrated the foolishness of the so-called 'politics of equilibrium', the Medicean doctrine of preventing one of the Italian principates from overwhelming the rest and uniting them under its hegemony.</p>
<p>Charles VIII's belligerence in Italy had made it transparent that the 'politics of equilibrium' did nothing but render the country unable to defend itself against a powerful invading force. Italy was shown to be very vulnerable to the predations of the powerful nation-states, France and Spain, that had forged themselves during the previous century. Alexander VI now followed the general tendency of all the princes of the day to crush the great feudatories and establish a centralized despotism. In this manner, he was able to take advantage of the defeat of the French in order to break the power of the Orsini. From that time on, Alexander was able to build himself an effective power base in the Papal States.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg/220px-Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg/330px-Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg/440px-Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1955" data-file-height="1537" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Castel_Sant%27Angelo_bild.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Castel_Sant%27Angelo" title="Castel Sant'Angelo">Castel Sant'Angelo</a> in Rome</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Virginio_Orsini" title="Virginio Orsini">Virginio Orsini</a>, who had been captured by the Spanish, died a prisoner at Naples, and the Pope confiscated his property. The rest of the Orsini clan still held out, defeating the papal troops sent against them under <a href="/wiki/Guidobaldo_da_Montefeltro" title="Guidobaldo da Montefeltro">Guidobaldo da Montefeltro</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Urbino" title="Urbino">Urbino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Borgia_(1474)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giovanni Borgia (1474)">Giovanni Borgia</a>, Duke of Gandia, at <a href="/wiki/Soriano_nel_Cimino" title="Soriano nel Cimino">Soriano</a> (January 1497). Peace was made through Venetian mediation, the Orsini paying 50,000 ducats in exchange for their confiscated lands; the Duke of Urbino, whom they had captured, was left by the Pope to pay his own ransom. The Orsini remained very powerful, and Pope Alexander VI could count on none but his 3,000 Spanish troops. His only success had been the capture of Ostia and the submission of the Francophile cardinals Colonna and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Savelli" title="Giovanni Battista Savelli">Savelli</a>.</p>
<p>Then occurred a major domestic tragedy for the house of Borgia. On 14 June, the Duke of Gandia, lately created Duke of <a href="/wiki/Benevento" title="Benevento">Benevento</a>, disappeared; the next day, his corpse was found in the Tiber.<sup id="cite_ref-Villari_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villari-17">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alexander, overwhelmed with grief, shut himself up in <a href="/wiki/Castel_Sant%27Angelo" title="Castel Sant'Angelo">Castel Sant'Angelo</a>. He declared that henceforth the moral reform of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Church</a> would be the sole object of his life. Every effort was made to discover the assassin, and suspicion fell on various highly placed people. Enquiries suddenly ceased without explanation. Cesare was suspected but not until much later and he was never named in the immediate aftermath, nor would there have been any particular reason for him to commit such a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-Villari_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villari-17">[14]</a></sup> The Orsini, against whom the Duke had been involved in the recent campaign, were the principal suspects at the time. The Duke had many other enemies. Ascanio Sforza, for example, had had a terrible row with him just a few days before the murder. No conclusive explanation was ever reached,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[23]</a></sup> and it may be that the crime was simply as a result of one of the Duke's sexual liaisons.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[Note 5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It is often alleged, sometimes by serious historians, that Alexander and his son, Cesare, poisoned Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Adriano_Castellesi" title="Adriano Castellesi">Adriano Castellesi</a>, but this is unlikely.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[Note 6]</a></sup> (When cardinals died, their wealth automatically reverted to the Church.) There is no evidence that the Borgias resorted to poisoning, judicial murder, or extortion to fund their schemes and the defense of the Papal States. The only contemporary accusations of poisoning were from some of the servants of the Borgias, extracted under torture by Alexander's bitter enemy and successor, <a href="/wiki/Julius_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Julius II">Julius II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Savonarola">Savonarola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Savonarola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg/170px-Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg/255px-Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg/340px-Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Girolamo_Savonarola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Savonarola" title="Girolamo Savonarola">Girolamo Savonarola</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The debased state of the curia was a major scandal. Opponents such as the powerful demagogic Florentine friar <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Savonarola" title="Girolamo Savonarola">Girolamo Savonarola</a> launched invectives against papal corruption and appealed for a general council to confront the papal abuses. Alexander is reported to have been reduced to laughter when Savonarola's denunciations were related to him. Nevertheless, he appointed <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Maggi" title="Sebastian Maggi">Sebastian Maggi</a> to investigate the friar, and he responded on 16 October 1495:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We are displeased at the disturbed state of affairs in Florence, the more so in that it owes its origin to your preaching. For you predict the future and publicly declare that you do so by the inspiration of the Holy Spirit when you should be reprehending vice and praising virtue. Such prophecies may easily lure the simple-minded away from the path of salvation and the obedience due to the Holy Roman Church. Prophecies like these should not be made when your charge is to forward peace and concord. Moreover, these are not the time for such teachings, calculated as they are to produce discord even in times of peace let alone in times of trouble. ... Since, however, we have been most happy to learn from certain cardinals and from your letter that you are ready to submit yourself to the reproofs of the Church, as becomes a Christian and a religious, we are beginning to think that what you have done has not been done with an evil motive, but from a certain simple-mindedness and a zeal, however misguided, for the Lord's vineyard. Our duty, however, prescribes that we order you, under holy obedience, to cease from public and private preaching until you are able to come to our presence, not under armed escort as is your present habit, but safely, quietly and modestly as becomes a religious, or until we make different arrangements. If you obey, as we hope you will, we for the time being suspend the operation of our former Brief so that you may live in peace in accordance with the dictates of your conscience.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[27]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The hostility of Savonarola seems to have been political rather than personal, and the friar sent a touching letter of condolence to the Pope on the death of the Duke of Gandia; "Faith, most Holy Father, is the one and true source of peace and consolation... Faith alone brings consolation from a far-off country."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[28]</a></sup> But eventually the Florentines tired of the friar's moralising and the Florentine government condemned the reformer to death (23 May 1498).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Familial_aggrandizement">Familial aggrandizement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Familial aggrandizement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In Italy at the time, the Spanish were looked down upon. Thus, the prominent Italian families looked down on the Borgia family, and they resented their power, which they sought for themselves. This is, at least partially, why both Pope Callixtus III and Pope Alexander VI gave powers to family members whom they could trust.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[Note 7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22,_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22%2C_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6520" data-file-height="5220" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_-_Bolla_%22Desiderando_nui%22,_dopo_il_18_settembre_1499_-_2951587.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Papal bull <i>Desiderando nui</i>, 1499</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In these circumstances Alexander, feeling more than ever that he could only rely on his own kin, turned his thoughts to further family aggrandizement. He had annulled Lucrezia's marriage to <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Sforza" title="Giovanni Sforza">Giovanni Sforza</a>, who had responded to the suggestion that he was impotent with the unsubstantiated counter-claim that Alexander and Cesare indulged in incestuous relations with Lucrezia, in 1497.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[Note 8]</a></sup> And, unable to arrange a union between Cesare and the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV_of_Naples" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick IV of Naples">King Frederick IV of Naples</a> (who had succeeded Ferdinand II the previous year), he induced Frederick by threats to agree to a marriage between the Duke of <a href="/wiki/Bisceglie" title="Bisceglie">Bisceglie</a>, a natural son of Alfonso II, and Lucrezia. Cesare, after resigning his cardinalate, was sent on a mission to France at the end of the year, bearing a bull of divorce for the new French king <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII_of_France" title="Louis XII of France">Louis XII</a>, in exchange for which he obtained the duchy of <a href="/wiki/Valentinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Valentinois">Valentinois</a> (a duchy chosen because it was consistent with his already known nickname of Valentino), a promise of material assistance in his schemes to subjugate the feudal princelings of papal Romagna, and a marriage to a princess of <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a>.</p>
<p>Alexander hoped that Louis XII's help would be more profitable to his house than that of Charles VIII had been. In spite of the remonstrances of Spain and of the Sforza, he allied himself with France in January 1499 and was joined by <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. By autumn Louis XII was in Italy expelling Lodovico Sforza from <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>. With French success seemingly assured, the Pope determined to deal drastically with the <a href="/wiki/Romagna" title="Romagna">Romagna</a>, which although nominally under papal rule was divided into a number of practically independent lordships on which Venice, Milan, and Florence cast hungry eyes. Cesare, empowered by the support of the French, began to attack the turbulent cities one by one in his capacity as nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Gonfalone_of_the_Church" title="Gonfalone of the Church">gonfaloniere</a></i> (standard bearer) of the church. But the expulsion of the French from Milan and the return of Lodovico Sforza interrupted his conquests, and he returned to Rome early in 1500.</p>
<h2><span id="The_Jubilee_(1500)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Jubilee_.281500.29">The Jubilee (1500)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The Jubilee (1500)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_(Christianity)" title="Jubilee (Christianity)">Jubilee year</a> 1500, Alexander ushered in the custom of opening a <a href="/wiki/Holy_door" title="Holy door">holy door</a> on Christmas Eve and closing it on Christmas Day the following year. After consulting with his Master of Ceremonies, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Burchard" title="Johann Burchard">Johann Burchard</a>, Pope Alexander VI opened the first holy door in <a href="/wiki/Old_St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Old St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a> on Christmas Eve 1499, and papal representatives opened the doors in the other three patriarchal basilicas. For this, Pope Alexander had a new opening created in the <i><a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">portico</a></i> of St. Peter's and commissioned a marble door. This door lasted until 1618, when another door was installed in <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">the new basilica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[Note 9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[Note 10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a ceremony similar to today's, Alexander was carried in the <i><a href="/wiki/Sedia_gestatoria" title="Sedia gestatoria">sedia gestatoria</a></i> to St. Peter's. He and his assistants, bearing candles, processed to the holy door, as the choir chanted <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biblica.com/en-us/bible/online-bible/?osis=nasb:Psalms.118:19–20:19">Psalm 118:19-20</a>. The Pope knocked on the door three times, workers moved it from the inside, and everyone then crossed the threshold to enter into a period of penance and reconciliation. Thus, Pope Alexander formalized the rite and began a longstanding tradition that is still in practice. Similar ceremonies were held at the other three basilicas.<sup id="cite_ref-holydoors_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holydoors-40">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alexander instituted a special rite for the closing of a holy door, as well. On the <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Feast of the Epiphany</a> in 1501, two cardinals began to seal the holy door with two bricks, one silver and one gold. <i>Sampietrini</i> (basilica workers)<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[Note 11]</a></sup> completed the seal, placing specially-minted coins and medals inside the wall.<sup id="cite_ref-holydoors_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holydoors-40">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery">Slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While the enterprising explorers of Spain and Portugal were quick to embrace the slavery practiced by the indigenous peoples they met in Africa and the New World,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[35]</a></sup> some popes spoke out against the practice. In 1435, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Eugene_IV" title="Pope Eugene IV">Pope Eugene IV</a> had issued an attack on slavery in his papal bull <i><a href="/wiki/Sicut_Dudum" title="Sicut Dudum">Sicut Dudum</a></i>, which included the excommunication of all those who engaged in the slave trade with the native chiefs. A form of <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">indentured servitude</a> was allowed, being similar to a peasant's duty to his <a href="/wiki/Homage_(feudal)" title="Homage (feudal)">liege lord</a> in Europe.</p>
<p>In the wake of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a>'s landing in the New World, Pope Alexander was asked by the Spanish monarchy to confirm their ownership of these newly found lands.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[36]</a></sup> The bulls issued by Pope Alexander VI: <i>Eximiae devotionis</i> (3 May 1493), <i><a href="/wiki/Inter_caetera" title="Inter caetera">Inter Caetera</a></i> (4 May 1493) and <i><a href="/wiki/Dudum_siquidem" title="Dudum siquidem">Dudum Siquidem</a></i> (23 September 1493), granted rights to Spain with respect to the newly discovered lands in the Americas similar to those <a href="/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V" title="Pope Nicholas V">Pope Nicholas V</a> had previously conferred with the bulls <i><a href="/wiki/Romanus_Pontifex" title="Romanus Pontifex">Romanus Pontifex</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dum_Diversas" title="Dum Diversas">Dum Diversas</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minnich_281_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minnich_281-49">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[39]</a></sup> Morales Padron (1979) concludes that these bulls gave power to enslave the natives.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[40]</a></sup> Minnich (2010) asserts that this "slave trade" was permitted to facilitate conversions to Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-Minnich_281_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minnich_281-49">[38]</a></sup> Other historians and Vatican scholars strongly disagree with these accusations and assert that Alexander never gave his approval to the practice of slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[41]</a></sup> Other later popes, such as <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Pope Paul III</a> in "Sublimus Dei" (1537), <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XIV" title="Pope Benedict XIV">Pope Benedict XIV</a> in <i>Immensa Pastorium</i> (1741), and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_XVI" title="Pope Gregory XVI">Pope Gregory XVI</a> in his letter <i>In Supremo Apostolatus</i> (1839), continued to condemn slavery.</p>
<p>Thornberry (2002) asserts that <i>Inter Caetera</i> was applied in the <i><a href="/wiki/Requerimiento" class="mw-redirect" title="Requerimiento">Requerimiento</a></i> which was read to American Indians (who could not understand the colonisers' language) before hostilities against them began. They were given the option to accept the authority of the Pope and Spanish crown or face being attacked and subjugated.<sup id="cite_ref-Thornberry_65_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thornberry_65-53">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[43]</a></sup> In 1993, the Indigenous Law Institute called on Pope John Paul II to revoke <i>Inter Caetera</i> and to make reparation for "this unreasonable historical grief". This was followed by a similar appeal in 1994 by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_World_Religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of World Religions">Parliament of World Religions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thornberry_65_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thornberry_65-53">[42]</a></sup> Despite their grandiose titles, the groups had little popular support and the requests were ignored.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_years">Last years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Last years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A danger now arose in the shape of a conspiracy by the deposed despots, the Orsini, and of some of Cesare's own <i><a href="/wiki/Condottieri" title="Condottieri">condottieri</a></i>. At first the papal troops were defeated and things looked bleak for the house of Borgia. But a promise of French help quickly forced the confederates to come to terms. Cesare, by an act of treachery, then seized the ringleaders at <a href="/wiki/Senigallia" title="Senigallia">Senigallia</a> and put <a href="/wiki/Oliverotto_da_Fermo" class="mw-redirect" title="Oliverotto da Fermo">Oliverotto da Fermo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitellozzo_Vitelli" title="Vitellozzo Vitelli">Vitellozzo Vitelli</a> to death (31 December 1502). When Alexander VI heard the news, he lured Cardinal Orsini to the Vatican and cast him into a dungeon, where he died. His goods were confiscated and many other members of the clan in Rome were arrested, while Alexander's son Goffredo Borgia led an expedition into the Campagna and seized their castles. Thus the two great houses of Orsini and Colonna, who had long fought for predominance in Rome and often flouted the Pope's authority, were subjugated and the Borgias' power increased. Cesare then returned to Rome, where his father asked him to assist Goffredo in reducing the last Orsini strongholds; this for some reason he was unwilling to do, much to his father's annoyance; but he eventually marched out, captured <a href="/wiki/Ceri" title="Ceri">Ceri</a> and made peace with Giulio Orsini, who surrendered <a href="/wiki/Bracciano" title="Bracciano">Bracciano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Villari_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villari-17">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The war between France and Spain for the possession of Naples dragged on, and the Pope was forever intriguing, ready to ally himself with whichever power promised the most advantageous terms at any moment. He offered to help Louis XII on condition that <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> be given to Cesare, and then offered to help Spain in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Siena" title="Siena">Siena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_(_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg/220px-Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg" width="220" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg/330px-Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg/440px-Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_%28_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2694" data-file-height="3944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tomb_of_Popes_Borja_(_Callisto_III_and_Alessandro_VI).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_extant_papal_tombs#15th_century" title="List of extant papal tombs">The tomb of Pope Alexander VI</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg/220px-Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg/330px-Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg/440px-Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2516" data-file-height="2009" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kmska_Titiaan_-_Jacopo_Pesaro_bisschop_van_Paphos_voorgesteld_door_paus_Alexander_VI_Borgia_aan_de_heilige_Petrus_-_28-02-2010_13-56-55.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Jacopo_Pesaro_being_presented_by_Pope_Alexander_VI_to_Saint_Peter" title="Jacopo Pesaro being presented by Pope Alexander VI to Saint Peter">Jacopo Pesaro being presented by Pope Alexander VI to Saint Peter</a></i>, painting by <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cesare_Borgia" title="Cesare Borgia">Cesare</a> was preparing for another expedition in August 1503 when, after he and his father had dined with Cardinal Adriano Castellesi on 6 August, they were taken ill with fever a few days later. Cesare, who "lay in bed, his skin peeling and his face suffused to a violet colour"<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[44]</a></sup> as a consequence of certain drastic measures to save him, eventually recovered; but the aged Pontiff apparently had little chance. <a href="/wiki/Johann_Burchard" title="Johann Burchard">Burchard's</a> <i>Diary</i> provides a few details of the pope's final illness and death:<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[45]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Saturday, the 12th of August, 1503, the Pope fell ill in the morning. After the hour of vespers, between six and seven o'clock a fever appeared and remained permanently. On the 15th of August thirteen ounces of blood were drawn from him and the <a href="/wiki/Tertian_ague" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertian ague">tertian ague</a> supervened. On Thursday, the 17th of August, at nine o'clock in the forenoon he took medicine. On Friday, the 18th, between nine and ten o'clock he confessed to the Bishop Gamboa of Carignola, who then read Mass to him. After his Communion he gave the Eucharist to the Pope who was sitting in bed. Then he ended the Mass at which were present five cardinals, Serra, Juan and Francesco Borgia, Casanova and Loris. The Pope told them that he felt very bad. At the hour of vespers after Gamboa had given him Extreme Unction, he died.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The pope was 72 years old.</p>
<p>As for his true faults, known only to his confessor, Pope Alexander VI apparently died genuinely repentant.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[Note 12]</a></sup> The bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Gallipoli" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Gallipoli">Gallipoli</a>, Alexis Celadoni, spoke of the pontiff's contrition during his funeral oration<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[Note 13]</a></sup> to the electors of Alexander's successor, pope <a href="/wiki/Pius_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius III">Pius III</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[Note 14]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>When at last the pope was suffering from a very severe sickness, he spontaneously requested, one after another, each of the last sacraments. He first made a very careful confession of his sins, with a contrite heart, and was affected even to the shedding of tears, I am told; then he received in Communion the most Sacred Body and Extreme Unction was administered to him.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Interregnum" title="Interregnum">interregnum</a> witnessed again the ancient "tradition" of violence and rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[Note 15]</a></sup> Cesare, too ill to attend to the business himself, sent <a href="/wiki/Micheletto_Corella" title="Micheletto Corella">Don Micheletto</a>, his chief <i>bravo</i>, to seize the Pope's treasures before the death was publicly announced. The next day the body was exhibited to the people and clergy of Rome, but was covered by an "old tapestry" ("antiquo tapete"), having become greatly disfigured by rapid decomposition. According to <a href="/wiki/Raffaello_Maffei" title="Raffaello Maffei">Raphael Volterrano</a>: "It was a revolting scene to look at that deformed, blackened corpse, prodigiously swelled, and exhaling an infectious smell; his lips and nose were covered with brown drivel, his mouth was opened very widely, and his tongue, inflated by poison, fell out upon his chin; therefore no fanatic or devotee dared to kiss his feet or hands, as custom would have required."<sup id="cite_ref-NC_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NC-69">[54]</a></sup> The Venetian ambassador stated that the body was "the ugliest, most monstrous and horrible dead body that was ever seen, without any form or likeness of humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-NC_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NC-69">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_von_Pastor" title="Ludwig von Pastor">Ludwig von Pastor</a> insists that the decomposition was "perfectly natural", owing to the summer heat.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[Note 16]</a></sup></p>
<p>It has been suggested that, having taken into account the unusual level of decomposition, Alexander VI was accidentally poisoned to death by his son, Cesare, with <a href="/wiki/Cantarella" title="Cantarella">cantarella</a> (which had been prepared to eliminate Cardinal Adriano), although some commentaries doubt these stories and attribute the Pope's death to <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, then prevalent in Rome, or to another such pestilence.<sup id="cite_ref-poison1_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poison1-30">[25]</a></sup> The ambassador of Ferrara wrote to Duke Ercole that it was no wonder the Pope and the duke were sick because nearly everyone in Rome was ill because of <a href="/wiki/Miasma_theory_of_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Miasma theory of disease">bad air</a> ("per la mala condictione de aere").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>After a short stay, the body was removed from the crypts of St. Peter's and installed in a less well-known church, the Spanish national church of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_in_Monserrato_degli_Spagnoli" title="Santa Maria in Monserrato degli Spagnoli">Santa Maria in Monserrato degli Spagnoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pope_Alexander_VI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
